  Mô tả: Lorena was supposed to die. She didn’t. Asher was the best contract killer money could buy — until the cancer diagnosis. When a corporation offers him a second life in a world governed by stats, classes, and levels, the deal is simple: transfer his soul into a new body, assassinate the most powerful mage in the kingdom, and live out his days free of pain. The transfer works. There’s just one problem with his new body — the farm girl he stole it from is still in there, and she’s furious. Now at level 9 and trapped with a voice in her head that won’t stop judging her, “Lorena” must claw her way through a world she doesn’t understand, join a crew of dangerous outcasts, and somehow close the gap between a pitchfork and the mage who’s already killed twelve of the best Adventurers before her. But the further she climbs, the harder it becomes to ignore the woman she wronged — and the cost of the deal that put her here. I still think you should have chosen Hunter over Rogue. You already took everything else from me. You could have given me that. Uploads daily until April 10th, then M/W/F! What to Expect: 1 - Weak to strong 2 - Fast pacing and gritty combat 3 - Dual consciousness MC 4 - 3rd person limited POV What NOT to Expect: 1 - Harem or romance 2 - wish fulfillment 3 - plot armor

To your right, I bet she sells hair ties. The girl’s smile was bright as Lorena stopped in front of her. She was the same girl she had bought the brush and polish from the day before. “Hi again, do you have any hair ties for sale?” The girl produced a small box of them in a variety of colors and thickness. Lorena picked up two, one yellow and one pale blue. The yellow one was thick and made of a soft fabric. The blue one was tight and elastic. Are you insane? What? Lorena looked at the hair ties in confusion. Those color choices are actually malicious. Ren said in a dramatic tone, almost pained. That’s a bit much for seven in the morning, Ren. Fine. Get all thin ones, they’ll keep your hair in place better. Choose the forest green, it’s your favorite, right? I already regret telling you that. Ren cackled. Grab the dark blue one too, that one will be the one thick one we get. What does thick versus thin do for us? My hair is a bit brittle and constantly being in a thin, tight ponytail is going to cause breakage. You can wear the thick one when you’re not busy being… you. Breakage, got it. That does sound painful. She could practically feel the eyeroll. Yes, and it makes our hair look terrible. Pick two of the burgundy, it’ll blend in with the blood I’m sure you’re going to get in my hair. Four? That seems excessive. Lorena intentionally ignored the jab about the blood. Trust me, you’ll lose three of them by the end of the month. How? I have a magical inventory to keep them in. It’s one of the great mysteries of the world. I think the System collects them while we sleep. Lorena chuckled, picked up the new colors, and paid. They were only 5 silver each thankfully. Lorena checked her map occasionally against the directions the clerk at the inn had given her. Thankfully, Ishal wasn’t working at the time. Once she was out of the square she quickly found the small nondescript building the clerk had described. The only thing inside was a large ornate gold frame that contained a shimmering pane of what appeared to be water, suspended in space. What is that? She asked Ren. Her instinct was to touch it, but that seemed risky. It’s a portal. You walk through it. Where does it take me? How should I know? Walk through and find out. Lorena circled it, finding no visible difference from any angle. Does it hurt? Ren paused, then spoke. I usually get a pretty bad headache, sometimes a nosebleed. Other than that though it’s not too bad. Lorena scrunched up her face, then walked with purpose through the portal and arrived in an entirely new world. Achievement: Don’t take the high road or the low road, take a portal Lorena looked around, then felt her nose. She looked at her fingertip but found no blood. I feel fine. Maybe I got lucky? If you discover it on Amazon, kindly report it. You were messing with me, weren’t you? An object flying in a wobbly pattern drew her shoulders tense. It took her a moment to process what it was: a book, flying through the air by flapping its covers. It flipped opened and several pages flew by until it landed on one that read. “Welcome to the Mage Quarter. Are you visiting or just passing through?” Lorena looked for a pen but didn’t see one, so she just answered out loud. “Passing through.” The book turned several pages, “Excellent! Enjoy your time in the Mage Quarter. Please be wary of the platforms, they do move.” And with that the book flew off, flapping its covers in the breeze. Lorena walked through the perfectly manicured grass until she arrived at the edge of a large cliff, no other path in sight. Just as she started looking for a bridge, a massive boulder leisurely floated across the canyon, several people standing on it. They all got off once the boulder arrived at the other side, and Lorena stepped on. She moved to the middle of the boulder, wary of any sudden movements knocking her off, but the boulder floated through the air smoothly. She walked a bit closer to the edge and peered over to see a waterfall of a shimmering liquid similar to the portal cascading down the cliff side into the abyss. This is so beautiful. Ren’s voice was full of wonder. It really is. Another golden frame sat in the middle of a field, a sign floating next to it read “Crafters’ Quarter”. Lorena entered the portal with more confidence this time around and returned to the world of Darnathal with its familiar limestone walls. The Crafters’ Quarter was similar to the Trade District, at least compared to the Mage Quarter. But instead of pristine cobblestone roads and vendors everywhere, the Crafters’ Quarter had large towering buildings and narrow streets, made even more narrow by displays and large signs that spilled out into the street. The signs glowed and pulsed, waves of Mana drawing her attention in every direction. An abrupt turn down a side street by Lorena caught Ren’s attention. What are you doing? Ren asked as Lorena slipped into Stealth. I just saw the elf from yesterday. The attractive concierge from the hotel? What? No—the one that was with the Mage, who stole from the vendors. Ren stirred. Okay, why are you following her? We need to see where she goes. The woman was getting too far away. Lorena dropped Stealth and jogged for a few seconds, trying to keep her footsteps light on the loud cobblestone street. She’s going to hear you! Get back in Stealth. It’s fine. Lorena said as she jogged a few more seconds and slipped into a recessed doorway. The elf stopped at that exact moment and scanned behind her. I knew I couldn’t trust you. It’s been an hour and you’re already breaking your promise. I am not. This was a spur of the moment thing. You still could have consulted with me before following a criminal down an alleyway. Lorena bit her tongue, literally. If I did that, she would have gotten away before we came to a decision. Sometimes you’re going to have to trust me too. Well that’s kind of hard to do when your choices always lead to violence and danger. Lorena ignored Ren for a moment, focusing on the Elven woman. She used Identify. Naith, Elven Hunter, Level 35 Damn, she was strong. Lorena’s shoulders tensed and she shuffled along in Stealth another few steps until Naith stopped, this time facing a side street that emptied into the alleyway. She had a bow on her back, but no pets. That seemed odd. A young child walked up to her and Naith knelt down. The girl was rail thin, cheeks sunken, belly distended from severe malnutrition. Lorena had seen that kind of hunger before in a few places she’d traveled for jobs—War zones, failed states, places she’d never want to return to. It surprised her that a place as prosperous as Everwind had children suffering like that in its capital city. Ren let out a small gasp as she took in the state of the girl. That poor thing. Naith did something with her hands, a mix between a finger snap and a flick of her wrist, and a four foot snake appeared. It had iridescent scales that glimmered in the sun. The young girl in front of Naith screamed and Lorena tensed, her hand reaching for her knife. But the girl smiled and reached out to pet the snake. “It licked me!” she yelled as the snake’s tongue flickered in and out of its mouth. “That means she likes you.” Lorena watched, crouched in Stealth behind a large crate, as Naith traded the girl a—a turkey leg? Her face lit up and she took a large bite out of the turkey leg, giggling with joy. “Thank you!” she said and ran off. Naith stood and stretched her back while her snake coiled itself up her body. Then she continued down the path. Can I keep following her? Fine. Lorena stalked the woman, dipping out of Stealth and jogging when she had cover. Naith stopped abruptly, let out a sigh, then vanished from existence. Does she have Stealth too? What just happened? Could have been a summon. It’s a Warlock thing, they have a spell to bring you to their location. Lorena turned around and walked for several minutes back up the alleyway before dropping Stealth. I’m sorry for not consulting you. She said to Ren, trying to keep things civil. Ren let out a small sigh. It’s okay. You were right, in the end. What kind of criminal feeds starving children? Complicated ones, Lorena said. They followed the map another few minutes until they arrived on a clearly residential street. Children’s toys littered the street, stray balls and what appeared to be the equivalent of a bicycle laid propped up against a wall. I could see Jade growing up here. Ren said. Lorena tried to picture it, but couldn’t. Then again, she didn’t exactly have a normal childhood as a frame of reference. She imagined she had more in common with the starving girl Naith fed than she did with Jade as a child. She pushed the thought away. Lorena came to a stop in the middle of the street and stared at a building to her left. It had a shabby wooden door, wear revealing several coats of paint that were all fading at different spots. Simple but worn shutters covered windows that concealed the inside from prying eyes. There was no address or name on the building, but a rectangular patch of fresher looking paint stood to the side of the door, like a number plaque had been removed. Lorena glanced at the rest of the homes on the street and found similar spots. Why would they all do that? So they couldn’t be identified, Lorena thought. Are you ready? Ren asked, excitement in her voice. The street was empty. She stepped up to the door and knocked three times.

  2. Boy Meets Beast

  Mô tả: Nobody is stupid enough to venture into unknown territories, except for Ilya. Don't get him wrong! He never meant to enter that mysterious village. Fate led him there to save, or be saved. "Peekaboo!" Beast is a cruel creature that used to be human. He loves playing childish games with his victims in the most terrifying and creepy ways imaginable. When Beast finds an exciting new toy named Ilya, he decides that he's never letting him go. Secrets unravel, unlikely allies unite to defeat a greater threat, and Ilya's accidental visit becomes more than just a horrible accident.

  09 | Slippery Slope
  https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/158305/boy-meets-beast/chapter/3200906/09-slippery-slope
───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Ilya waited until Charlie was out of sight, way up the stairs, then hurried along that long corridor where he saw what he thought was a side door that would lead him out of this shithole. His footsteps were swift but quiet. Who knows what kind of freak Charlie was; he might hear him and tear him apart. His watch abruptly beeped, causing him to jump. "Shit, shit, shit," he muttered as he grappled with his device to shut it up. The device stopped beeping. The number on the screen was 60. It wasn't as low as Ilya thought it would be by now. Maybe that drink Charlie gave him helped a bit, but still, Ilya was pushing his luck. He was running on fumes. With his heart pounding insanely in his little chest, Ilya reached the side door and grabbed the handle. He twisted it, but to his disappointment, it was locked. And the key was nowhere to be found. "Fuck." Time was running out. Charlie could be on his way down any minute now. Ilya returned to the living room and tried to open the front door. He barely managed to get a hold of the handle with his sweaty jittery hands. Of course, the door was still locked. It jiggled a bit, making a slight sound that frightened him. Ilya gaped at the stairs, hoping Charlie didn't hear that. Still no sign of the big guy. Ilya took a deep breath, then scanned around the door, left and right, up and down. He looked back up and found the key on a screw above the door. However, it was hanging way up for him to reach, but far enough for giant Charlie to reach. Ilya gritted his teeth and quietly cursed. Then he turned around and found something that would help him reach the key—a sofa chair right next to the couch he had napped on. With a weak grip from both hands, Ilya began pulling the chair to the door. Once it moved, small creatures ran out from under it, squealing and scattering everywhere. "Eek!" Ilya yelped and jumped away. He suppressed a squeak of revulsion behind a pout. His hands raised stiffly and shook in disgust. Those icky rats scrambled in every direction, fully occupying the living room before they disappeared behind other pieces of furniture. This house was full of trash, mold, cockroaches, and now rats! One of them even crawled on his shoe. "Oh, God." Ilya swallowed bitterly. "That's so gross." This story has been unlawfully obtained without the author's consent. Report any appearances on Amazon. When the shock of revulsion wore off, Ilya continued dragging the chair to the desired location. It only took a couple more pulls, and Ilya was able to climb it and take the key. "Yes," he excitedly whispered. He hopped down and quickly inserted the key in the keyhole, twisting it and finally unlocking the front door. Ilya wasted no time running out of that place, leaving the door open behind him. It was freezing outside. Soft powdery snow started to fall, carried by the December wind. The sun had set beyond the dark horizon. The town looked peaceful at night, with little lighting and no shooter to disrupt its serenity. Ilya trailed his way back to the train station. It took him some time, but he found it. It wasn't hard to miss in this small town. Then suddenly, a terrifying roar came from the direction of Charlie's house. "Jesus Christ!" Ilya gasped and ran as fast as he could until he was standing on the platform. He looked left and right and saw the headlights of a coming train. He glanced over his shoulder, expecting Charlie to be right behind him. Out of breath and shaking in the wintry weather, Ilya hugged himself and waited. "Come on, come on, come on." Ilya feared that the train wouldn't arrive in time. Then he remembered his phone! He dropped it around here somewhere. Ilya quickly got on all four and started searching the lightly white-covered ground. His hands turned pink from touching the cold snow as he swiped them on the platform, helplessly trying to find his phone. He saw a light reflecting on something next to his hand. He moved his hand and touched that thing. A shaky sound came out of Ilya's throat that sounded like something between a cry and a laugh. He found it. He found his phone. Ilya started laughing with tears. He swiped the snow from the screen, but it was black. His phone must have shut down from the cold. Ilya pressed the power button on the side and waited for his phone to start back up. As soon as it turned on, a flashing warning showed up on the screen. 'Battery 0%.' Then it turned off again. "Aaaah!" Ilya let out a scream of frustration. "Gimme a fucking break!" The engine's rattling was getting nearer. Ilya spun to see that it was only seconds away from arriving. The ground vibrated under his feet. He slipped his phone in his pocket and got up. His leg was pouncing nervously as he remained there defenselessly while a crazy person was tracking him down. Ilya watched his surroundings just in case Charlie was near. He thought he saw something move behind him, but maybe it was just his anxiety taking over. He couldn't hear anything but the loud rumbling of the train. Ilya shook his head when the images around him blurred. He was getting dizzy again. He almost lost his balance but spread his legs to pin his feet on the ground and keep himself from collapsing. The train arrived and slowly stopped. Ilya got closer. His breathing accelerated as the anticipation of finally escaping was intense. Once the doors opened, Ilya beamed and grabbed one of the doors to pull himself in. "Oh, thank God." Ilya climbed in, but before his foot could touch the floor of his ride, something grabbed him. "No!" A familiar gruff voice shouted. "Wrong train!" A painful grasp yanked the boy right out of the train and sent him falling onto the concrete floor. Ilya gasped, feeling his back ribs cracking and knocking the air out of his lungs. All Ilya could see as he was falling were the white snowy clouds in the sky. Snowflakes danced their way onto his flushed cheeks. Some lay on his heavy lashes as they steadily moved to cover his eyes. His head took a heavy blow that left him dazed. He lay there, not moving. His eyes were weary as he wheezed and suffered the impact of the fall. A giant blurry figure stooped over him. "Ah, bloody hell! Did I hurt you?" And that was the last thing Ilya saw before passing out.

  10 | Hairy Nightmare

Ilya had a dream, or what he thought was a dream. He was back at Charlie's house, lying on that filthy couch. It was as if he never left. But something was different this time. The house was too quiet, or so it seemed at first. Then Ilya's ear caught a weird noise coming from outside the house. No. Not one sound, but many. A lot more. Ilya heard people moaning. They roamed around the house, wailing, some screaming. Their voices got louder, closer. Ilya couldn't tell if they were in pain or insane, but they scared him. They reminded him of the sound coming out of that faceless man's throat. Ilya's attempt to move and sit up was in vain. The back of his head was throbbing. His limbs were weak. His eyes were heavy. It felt like he was in a state between sleep and waking. Then something, or someone, moved into the living room. Ilya slowly moved his tired eyes to see that he was not alone anymore. He saw someone with a cowboy hat and a long coat—Charlie's trench coat. Charlie's tall frame was hunched over, turning his back to Ilya and his eyes on the front door. His arms were raised on both sides as if he were about to perform a jump attack. "Ch... Charlie?" Ilya said, wearily. "Shhh," Charlie said, turning halfway until the side of his face was visible. "Do ye hear that?" Ilya blinked a few times until Charlie's fuzzy image became clear. This book was originally published on Royal Road. Check it out there for the real experience. It seemed like Charlie's grey beard got thicker and longer. The side of his face, his hands, and his feet became hairier. Then Ilya noticed that Charlie wasn't just hunching over. He was anticipating, excited even; like a predator about to hunt for dinner. The front door banged as the creatures gathered there. Eerie throaty sounds made Ilya gasp. Next, the windows rattled. "It's the dead," Charlie said, his voice getting deeper. "They're everywhere." Charlie ditched his coat and unbuttoned his shirt, eyes never leaving that door. "They know you're here." Charlie tilted his head toward Ilya. "Those bastards followed your blood trail." Ilya could feel his heartbeats running faster. It wasn't only Charlie's excitement that scared him; it was how his body gradually morphed in front of him. First, it was those eyes; Ilya could have sworn he witnessed them glow like cat eyes in the dark. Charlie's smile got bigger, showing teeth too white and too sharp to be human. His body was already hairy, but it got hairier by the second until a coat of fur covered every inch of him. Then Ilya heard a shocking sound coming from Charlie's bones; they were cracking as they moved inside him, changing his shape. Charlie growled in pain as he grew taller. His back curved and hunched over like an animal. Thick claws cut through the tip of his fingers, replacing his nails. Then the bones in his feet shuffled, elevating the back of them above the ground, while the front of them turned into paws. Charlie groaned with a monstrous voice, "Don't fret, lad." He raised his head and roared as his mouth shifted into a long maw full of fangs. Ilya's eyes shot open when he realized what Charlie had become. A werewolf! When Charlie fully transformed, he looked at Ilya with bright yellow eyes and smiled. His wolf form was beyond terrifying. If Ilya was afraid of Charlie's giant human form, then this form would give him nightmares for the rest of his miserable short life. Then, with a spine-chilling inhumanly deep voice, Charlie declared, "I'll protect you." Ilya's breathing got faster. He closed his eyes and prayed that this nightmare would end soon. He prayed that he would wake up. He prayed and prayed. Wake up! Wake up, now!

The stench had been faint before, but now that he was sitting still it was becoming impossible to ignore. It was thick and sour, the kind of smell that made his stomach twist. His eyes slowly shifted toward the corner of the cell. There sat a small wooden bucket. Dean stared at it for a moment before Will's memories filled in the rest. The answer was unpleasantly simple. That bucket was the prisoners' latrine. The place where anyone locked in the cell had to relieve themselves. And it would remain there until a guard eventually bothered to empty it. Sometimes that happened once a day. Sometimes it didn't. Dean pinched the bridge of his nose and let out a quiet groan. 'Fuck Stark… fuck Winterfell.' His gaze drifted toward the iron bars of the cell. 'If that bastard doesn't take me out of this shitty cell within a day… I'm bailing out.' He meant every word. Dean might have been desperate enough to bluff a lord of the North to save his life, but he still had limits. A modern man like him was not going to sit quietly in a filthy medieval prison for long. He had his standards. In his previous life he had already spent far too much time confined to a bed.   CH 6. A Lord's Dilemma

"To contact the Old Gods again," Dean said, voicing his thoughts, "I will need to perform a ritual in the godswood." At the same time, another thought ran beneath his words. This was not just about convincing Ned. It was a chance to test his ability. The rules of Shadow Extraction were still unclear in practice. It clearly stated that he had to personally kill the target, though his shadows could assist him. But what counted as "personally"? Did he need to fight the creature from start to finish himself, relying only on his shadows? Or could other people, apart from him and his shadows, weaken the target first, bringing it to the brink of death, and then he would step in to deliver the final killing blow? If the second option worked… that would change everything. It would mean he could turn powerful beasts into shadow soldiers without risking his life fighting them head-on. And this so-called ritual… it was the perfect excuse. If Ned agreed, Dean could have multiple strong creatures brought to him alive but weakened. All he would need to do was land the final blow. If that counted as "his kill"… Then he could gain powerful shadow soldiers right here in Winterfell. The thought alone was enough to make the risk worth it. "A ritual?" Ned asked as a faint crease appeared between his brows. Dean nodded confidently. "It requires sacrifice," he said. "Of animals and birds. Creatures that must be offered before the heart tree with my own hands." Ned's eyebrows drew together as a frown appeared on his face,"What creatures?" Dean listed them carefully, watching Ned's face for the slightest twitch. "A northern elk, a northern garron, a falcon, an auroch and a bear." "They must be brought alive," Dean pressed, sensing the wall of Northern tradition closing in around him. "Half-broken. Weak enough that the life leaves them slowly under the weirwood. The Old Gods favor the strong, my lord. The stronger the beast, the clearer the truth." Disgust and revulsion appeared on Ned's face as he heard that. "That is the blood-work of red priests and the maegi of the south," he said. "My gods are silent. They watch. They do not demand the torture of beasts to whisper secrets in a man's ear. He said that if I go south, I will not return. He also said that these coming days will be turbulent, and that harm may come not only to me but to those I hold dear." That last part hung heavily in the air between them. Catelyn's face changed at once, concern turning into something sharper. "Then you must not go," she said firmly, stepping closer to him. "If there is even a chance that what he says is true, you cannot risk it. Winterfell needs you, your family needs you, and the North is safer with you here." Ned listened to her, his expression steady but troubled. "If Robert asks me to serve, I cannot simply refuse him," he replied. "He is my king, and more than that, he is my friend. If he rides all this way to ask for my help, then something is wrong. Jon Arryn is dead, and Robert may stand alone in a court full of men he does not fully trust." Catelyn shook her head slightly, her voice carrying both worry and frustration. "And what of us?" she asked. "What of your children? If there is danger in King's Landing, then walking into it willingly would place all of us at risk." Ned stepped closer to her. But I will not act blindly. If I go, I will go with caution, and I will not take anyone except for Sansa with me." He hesitated before adding, "I would rather keep her here. The capital is not a place I trust." He looked at Catelyn and continued, "But Robert has already spoken of joining our houses. Sansa is to be promised to his son. If I leave her behind, it will be seen as disrespect to the king and the queen." Catelyn frowned at once. "She is still a child, Ned. You are taking her into a dangerous place." Ned's voice lowered. "If anything goes wrong, I will make sure she has a way to leave safely. I will not let her be trapped there." The room fell quiet as his words settled. Catelyn looked at him for a long moment, her worry clear in her eyes. Ned reached out and hugged her. Neither of them spoke after that.   Mô tả: In 2025 the world discovered the existence of qi. This lead to the development of Formations, Techniques, and Talismans, as technological development gave way to the development of cultivation. The health of every human was greatly improved and the quality of life increased. In 2050, however, the problems began. People from another world started arriving, seeking to exploit this newly "Awakened" world, and the people of Earth must fight to protect themselves against the cultivators from higher realms which keep coming through the various gates around the world.

The Ambassador looked down to see the swarming army and noticed Kevin collapsed on the ground. He hesitated for a second, wondering if he should fly the man to a medical area, when a giant gorilla arm hit his cheek, knocking him backwards by ten meters. He would just have to leave Kevin for the others to deal with, or the enemy in front of him might send him to join Kevin. With virtually unlimited energy which replenished faster than he could use it, she was being pushed backwards. Those too were definitely more than just master and apprentice, though he knew not to judge them for it. They were both consenting adults, after all. He’d been learning to accept unusual relationships for decades, ever since his hippy daughter returned from Woodstock with a girlfriend. Sure, they were different species, but he’d seen plenty of interracial relationships before. He then realized how bad that sounded. He was trying to say that he didn’t care that they were different species, because they were both intelligent adults who consented. He definitely didn’t have a problem with different humans doing the same, regardless of which continent their ancestors were from. ‘I’m just going to assume those thoughts are from the concussion.’ he thought, as he focused on a technique that he had never needed to use before. In the Ji family library he had be shown a healing technique which could use any type of qi, just working slightly better with some verities. It could take organic materials from any lifeform around, alive or dead, and adjust it to mesh properly with your own flesh. You could then absorb it into your body and use it to replace damaged parts. It used far too much qi to use it to heal minor injuries, and far more if the enemy was alive or had decent qi densities, as actively moving qi disrupted the technique, but he should be able to use it to heal himself in this situation. After all, many of the bodies around him were from stone chimpanzees, which were very similar to humans, so the qi usage should only be around 1% of what it would be if he had to use grass or weeds or wood as the raw material. Of course, if he was actually a stone chimpanzee like he was pretending to be, he could likely just graft their tissue onto himself directly, only needing to guarantee that it didn’t cause an immune response, but this would work for now. As the individual cells of the bodies around him started to evaporate off of the corpses, only to be adjusted and fly onto his face, he used a bit of telekinesis to put the bones of his jaw back where they should be. The drama above kept the two main enemies busy over the minute or so it took him to heal, and he stood there, all of the qi he could manage to use swirling around him, gathering the flesh and bone of his enemies and protecting him against enemies that got too close. ‘At least the fact that their skin was vaporized if they touched the barrier caused them to find other enemies’, he mused as the last of his replacement skin was grafted on. He spent a few seconds trying to plan the battle which would soon resume. The armies which were storming the base would keep those on the ground busy, but he would need to deal with the ones in the air. Either of them could quickly wipe out the attackers, so he needed to keep them busy. ‘This would be much easier if I was still a Nascent.’ he thought, then realized that he might be able to make that happen. After all, his current foundation was far stronger than that of his old body. Its biological age was probably in its late twenties, haven’t aged by a decade or so after he took over due to the excessive use of Rebirth to repair all of the genetic damage caused by the cloning procedure. If cloning was going to become routine, they would need to find a better way to make human clones. Had been able to cultivate a much stronger foundation than in his hundred year old body, partly because of the younger body being more resilient and partly because his current technique was far better than the one the military had given him starting two decades ago. Souls were able to keep their qi reserves at around eighty percent full once awakened, by drawing in qi particles directly from higher dimensional space, though the now dormant state had lowered that to around fifty percent. When it was fully awake he could use that connection to higher dimensions to create portals among other things, but since possessing a clone of his old body his soul had essential been dreaming, unable to wake up due to an insufficient body. It was like a diabetic going into a coma from insufficient blood sugar which was needed for the brain to function. Now that he was at the peak of level four, however, he might be able to wake it up. He started drawing out qi and feeding it back into the soul, incorporating his memories of his past lives to try and recreate the situation of his initial breakthrough. As he did so, the memories started flowing into his mind more and more quickly, reminding him of details he had long forgot. He even remembered being a woman in a past life, as well as being a roman senator with an attraction to other men. This made him even more disgusted with himself for thinking anything was wrong with atypical relationships, but he tried to ignore it and feed even more memories into the soul. After another ten seconds, there was a shift inside of him as his soul became fully aware of the world around it, and qi began to flood into it from beyond normal space and time as it expanded slightly to accommodate his new understanding and body. Which also means buying or renting a building to work in. With enough work, though, you could have a core ‘US Armed Forces’ version, plus a supplement for each division. Maybe the Marines book has ways to boost damage at the expense of burning out quicker, the Army is about lasting as long as possible, the Air Force is about aerial combat and faster flight, the Marines are about naval and maybe underwater warfare, and the Space Force is about functioning in a vacuum and surviving in hostile environments, like radioactive areas.’ As he thought about it he nodded. There was a bright flash of light and we appeared on a different platform, surrounded by a different set of walls and soldiers. ‘That is actually cheaper than most military projects, but a new training method could be far more useful than a new tank or jet at this point. Let me think it over a bit more, see if I can convince the Pentagon to release a few million to start the project, then we can increase funding based on performance.’ I nodded and we stepped off the platform. “So.” I said nodding, pretending that we hadn’t just had a conversation. “We need to leave tomorrow morning, right? What do we need to do in town today?” He looked around as we left the array area. “Well, I need to take a letter to the Ji family estate, then we’ll need to go to the White Tiger sect and pick up the beasts we ordered.” I nodded. “Well, I have some things to sell them as well, plus I’d like to stop by a book store owned by one of them to get some jade copies made. I bought a few level two occupation manuals in Crystal Summit, and I think they would sell well here.” After a slight pause I telepathically added, ‘You might also consider giving a copy of Chimera’s manual to the White Tiger sect. It fits the Beast Tamer theme well, and if they had a level five elder they would have far more influence in the area, which could greatly improve how well their PR campaign goes.’ He nodded and we made our way to Ji Cha’s book store. Once inside I introduced the Ambassador. “We have several jade slips we’d like copied, if you don’t mind. We can pay with stones or you can just make a few extra copies to sell as payment.” Ji Cha nodded. “It depends on how well I think the books will sell, but I don’t mind making copies.” On the table against the wall behind him there was a glass box which contained the treasure caterpillars I had sold him. They appeared to be doing well, and one of them was even in the process of building a cocoon. It must have been close to transforming when it was caught. I pulled out all of the level two occupation manuals, and he started looking through them. “Puppet Master Guide? Orchard guide? Artifact Crafter’s Guide? These are good manuals. The Artifact Crafting one in particular. There’s a guild that covers that in town, but it has a monopoly on most of the artifacts around here, which is why we have to import. If we can bring in designs from outside, though, they can’t claim that we stole theirs.” I nodded. “Well, I already checked. It does have the design for a type of storage bag and beast bag which, though not identical to the ones they make, should have descent performance. No storage ring, though. That’s probably in the level three version, called ‘Relic Crafter’s Guide’, but I didn’t get a copy of that. Next time I’m in Crystal Summit though, I’ll pick up the rest of the level two manuals they have and the few level threes.” He nodded. “In that case, I have a proposal. I will make you copies of all of these jades for free. I will also give you ten percent of any future sales of these books. In exchange, I want permission to make as many copies as I want. I doubt the Artifact Crafter’s Guild will complain too loudly, but having a backer always helps.” The Ambassador spoke up. “In that case, can you tell me what the highest level in the guild is?” “Level four, I think? That would be the guild head. Being a member of the Ji family might be enough that he doesn’t cause me any trouble, as the local head is level five, but he’s unlikely to get involved in something so small, so the Guild head might cause some issues.” The Ambassador smiled. “In that case, I’ll be the backer as well. I recently advanced to level five, so if they cause you trouble, tell them Yu Fei has an interest in those books.” He released enough aura to show that he wasn’t lying, and Ji Cha instantly froze in fear. “Woah, boss. He’s only peak level one. That’s a bit much.” I said, helping Ji Cha back onto his stool from where he fell off. “Oh, sorry about that.” Several other people in the store paused as well, then looked weary. The Ambassador noticed this and apologized to them as well. “I was just verifying that I was at that level. I’m not going to hurt anyone.” A few mortals and level ones nervously nodded, mumbled something about coming back later, then left. The three level twos and one level one, however, just looked at each other, then went back to shopping. After Ji Cha calmed down, he nodded. “In that case, would you also accept ten percent of the sales of these books?” he asked. The Ambassador nodded. “That’s fine. Also, would you mind making me a copy of this book? I don’t mind if you sell them to the White Tiger sect, as I’m about to give them a copy, but please don’t sell to others without my permission.” He pulled out the book he got from Chimera and placed it on the table. Ji Cha picked the book up and flipped through it. “At least ten layers of writing, twelve in some places. I can do it, but to make a book at this level will take at a few days, maybe more. I would also need to make at least twenty copies or charge you a large part of the cost of a High grade level five manual, at least one hundred thousand, for a one time print.” The Ambassador nodded. “In that case, I’ll pay for the entire run now. Just send the copies and the original to the White Tiger sect when you are finished with them, and they can send me the ones they don’t need.” He motioned towards his bag, but I held up a hand, realizing how he was going to pay. “Maybe you should make such a large payment in a more secure way?” I suggested. “Perhaps do it through the Ji family estate, who can handle such a large transactions?” I then sent the Ambassador a telepathic warning, that pulling out a cube worth over seven hundred thousand stones in public might cause some alarm. “You’re right. We should go to the estate to finish this.” he said, and after Ji Cha informed his assistant we left.

  Mô tả: Kai, the true genius behind the world-dominating game Endless, was betrayed by his partner and left to rot. Reconstructed as a "Glitch" who defies the system's physics, he hides as a powerless miner in a dystopian future. While the world worships the new "Heroes," Kai gathers resources to activate a developer’s backdoor, beginning his secret ascent to reclaim his world and destroy those who stole it.

  The Enduring Cadaver

[THE STAIRCASE TO FLOOR 4] The staircase spiraled upward, claustrophobic and dark, like the inside of a throat swallowing them whole. Each step exhaled centuries of stale dust. Each breath tasted of sulfur and something older—a sweet, sickening rot that existed long before language was invented to accuse it. Kai walked first. His pace was measured, unhurried, and absolute. Behind him, Jie could not match the rhythm. The young disciple's steps stumbled, caught in the agonizing space between resolve and regret. He gripped his wooden sword until the leather hilt squealed under the pressure of his white knuckles. "How is the Fourth Floor?" Kai asked, his eyes fixed on the dark ascent. "Is it difficult?" The words tore loose from Jie's chest. "Alone." Kai glanced back over his shoulder. Jie was fifteen. Far too young to be carrying survivor's guilt like a suit of ceremonial armor. "Why come here at all?" Kai asked. Jie hesitated. Because I ran. The truth lodged in his throat like a swallowed bone. Instead, he forced out the other truth. "Master K believed the Dungeon held 'The Truth.' He thought if he found it… he could understand why the outside world is decaying." Kai stopped. The Truth. Not power. Not gold. Not legendary weapons. The old martial artist had come searching for the source code of the collapse. A faint shadow crossed Kai's expression—not surprise, but a grim recognition. "He was looking in the only place it would hide," Kai murmured. Ahead, the iron doors of the Fourth Floor loomed. They were massive, blackened, and covered in thick, pulsing ridges—veined like a diseased heart left to calcify in the dark. Jie's steps died completely. Courage drained visibly from his shoulders. What if he's dead? What if he's disappointed I came back? Kai stepped back down. He reached out, placing a firm, heavy hand on the boy's head. It was warm. Grounding. "Don't fear," Kai said. No. The thought battered uselessly against invisible restraints. Something freezing and absolute was coiled around his spine, puppeteering his nervous system. Protect me. The memory dimmed. The cold stone crawled further across K's cheek, threatening to consume his eye. No. Not yet. Kai lunged again. Master K's arm moved automatically, chambering a perfect, Ki-infused killing strike aimed at the boy's heart. Inside his own mind, K roared. STOP. The corruption tightened its grip, forcing the fist downward. But for the first time since the stone took him, something inside Master K did not beg to survive. It did not fear the dark. His fist trembles. It chose to resist. Even if resistance meant shattering.

  Mô tả: After 10,000 years perfecting a single pill, Bai Fanxian emerges from seclusion to find the world has moved on without her.   Chapter 136 An Elixir That Lets You Use Magic!
  https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/136271/the-alchemy-empress-10000-years-later/chapter/3196367/chapter-136-an-elixir-that-lets-you-use-magic

*THUD!* Huang Zihuan set both of them down on the beach not far from Bai Fanxian. Li Xinmei still looked regretful. For ordinary people, flying through the air was a dream almost everyone had at least once. Even cultivators pushed themselves toward Grandmaster level partly for that: the experience of true, unrestrained flight. "Leader, is it really impossible for me to cultivate?" Chunfeng asked, trying to keep the hope out of his voice. His eyes were still on the cleared ground where Bai Fanxian had moved a forest in a few gestures. "It's not that it's impossible." She murmured. That alone was enough to bring him a step closer. "You're serious?" "But I don't recommend it." He went still. She continued: "Your body can still generate a qi core. But the meridians in your arms and legs are completely severed. Even if you force yourself to cultivate, I think the chances of success are less than minimal." "..." "So I'd point you toward something called magic instead. Which is why you came today, isn't it?" "But magic is..." He couldn't honestly say he didn't believe in it. Chunfeng had worked in the government's special unit long enough to know something like this existed. The difference between magic and qi, though, was that people who could genuinely use magic were nearly nonexistent. Not just in this country. Even if you searched the entire West, the odds of finding a real magic user were practically zero. So he had heard of it. He had never encountered it. "You know the military was holding someone at the Eastern Base." Bai Fanxian was referring to Barbatos. Chunfeng knew about it, at least in broad terms. She stood there with the same expression she might use to describe what she had for breakfast, as if extracting mana from a person and turning it into medicine was a perfectly ordinary afternoon's work. It occurred to him that he had forgotten her title. Because in all the time since they'd met, she hadn't done anything that matched it — not in front of him. The Alchemy Empress. Bai Fanxian's most remarkable quality had never been her appearance or her overwhelming power. It was this — the alchemical art that had made her name in the first place. You could be reading stolen content. Head to Royal Road for the genuine story. "Could I see it?" The question was out before he thought about it. Then his expression shifted, because he realized what he had just casually done. In the alchemist world, a person's formulas and elixirs were guarded as carefully as their lives. Asking to see one this offhandedly could get you permanently cut off by some alchemists. "Here." She showed not the slightest offense. She simply tossed the pill to him without a second thought. In his palm sat a clean white elixir pill with pale blue mana currents drifting around it, glittering faintly like a scattering of stars. He stared at it for about five seconds before he noticed everyone was looking at him. "That's still an experimental version." "...I see. That's a shame." Chunfeng moved to hand it back. She didn't take it. Instead, she said the same thing again. "That's still an experimental version..." "Yes, I understood you the first time." He nodded slowly. But something was clicking into place as he caught the flat, patient stare Bai Fanxian had fixed on him — the look of someone waiting for the obvious to sink in. Or was it — "...You want me to be a test subject, don't you?" "Those are your words." She didn't confirm it. She didn't deny it either. Whether inviting Chunfeng to the island had, from the beginning, been partly about testing this newly refined elixir. That was something only she knew. "What does it do?" An elixir that let you use magic. It sounded like something out of a story. But hearing it from the woman called the Alchemy Empress, it felt, somehow, entirely believable. "Chief..." Li Xinmei had a feeling her chief was about to walk into something. That strange glowing pill did not look like something safe to eat. "Understood." He turned to Bai Fanxian, who stood watching in complete calm, as though this were proceeding exactly as expected. She hasn't moved. So it must be fine. That conclusion was enough. The elderly butler reached out and gently lifted Li Xinmei away from Chunfeng — whose condition was becoming dangerous to anyone nearby. "Is he going to be alright?" Li Xinmei was still frightened, but when she remembered what these two were capable of, she managed to steady herself. She turned back and asked with cautious hope. "..." Bai Fanxian didn't answer. Instead, she walked toward Chunfeng, who had begun to sink toward the ground. The strain visible on his face made it clear. Whatever was in this pill was not something to be taken lightly. "Mm..." She murmured, as if turning something over in her mind. Then her fingers rose and pressed gently to the center of his forehead. A bright white light bloomed in the same instant. It expanded outward, enclosing his body in a luminous shell. Huang Zihuan, standing nearby, felt the pressure radiating from within like something vast pressing outward against its container. "...!" Through his connection to the Border, the old man could sense clearly what was building. He watched the white light shoot upward in a pillar toward the sky. From somewhere in the center of it, he heard a sound like something being unmade and reborn. "HAAAH!" The shout came up from deep in Chunfeng's chest and broke through the air. Then silence. The white light began to scatter. It fractured like glass and came apart in glittering fragments that caught the sunlight as they fell. Chunfeng stood at the center of it, eyes closed. Like the main character of a scene written specifically for him. The stillness in his expression said he was holding onto this moment for as long as it would last. But then — "...Chief?" Li Xinmei noticed something wrong. More than two minutes had gone by. He still hadn't moved. She stepped closer. Her hand reached out — *THUD!* Chunfeng fell backward, stiff as stone. His eyes had rolled back, barely open. A thin line of foam had appeared at the corner of his mouth. "Chief!!" "..." Li Xinmei crouched beside him immediately, checking his condition with the conscientiousness of a good subordinate. Meanwhile, Huang Zihuan turned to look at his lady — who had somehow produced a notebook and pen from nowhere. "...Mm. Sample one — failed." Bai Fanxian made a note on the page with perfect composure, paying no attention to her butler's expression. "My lady..." Huang Zihuan smiled dryly. Something in her manner suggested she had already guessed it might go this way. She didn't look surprised. She looked exactly like someone whose suspicion had just been confirmed. And then — "Judging by his state, he should wake up in three days... Now, how do I coax him into taking sample two?"

The answer was the dense life force flowing through this area. It was one of the quiet advantages of being a patient in Bai Fanxian's clinic. You didn't need to eat normally here.   Mô tả: Lianthorn Belladonna could have been so many things. An artist, a mage, a gardener. Instead, his family sealed his future, trapping him in a life of scheming, poison, and murder. He’s through with it. On the cusp of completing his poisonous masterpiece, Lianthorn makes a choice that will change everything. He flees the gilded cage of their family manor and seeks refuge in a quiet town on the outskirts of civilization, where the name Belladonna means nothing. With his family’s infamous scarlet-bound recipe book hidden away, he attempts to forget the toxins and discover the simple joy of helping people. But out on the frontier and in the company of a red-scaled Draconian working as a carpenter in spite of her fire powers, ‘helping people’ will require all his skills. Including the alchemy he worked so hard to escape. Lianthorn abandoned everything he’d ever known to gain his freedom. Now, to flourish in his new life, he’ll have to learn a whole new way of living and maybe, just maybe, discover the recipe for love along the way.

  Chapter 174: Defensive Maneuvers
  https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/135311/alchemist-of-the-wilds-an-ex-assassins-guide-to/chapter/3200133/chapter-174-defensive-maneuvers
───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

It was an odd feeling, to find myself standing not far from our house in a wide open area in front of a large group of people who’d elected to help protect my family and home of their own volition, no badgering, bribes or threats required. They certainly had their reasons. Swiftband was their home, too. However, they could have ever so easily chosen not to lift a finger and let the Wild Hunt have what they wanted before hopefully moving on and leaving the town unmolested. The chances of that weren’t exactly good, but it was still a possibility. Regardless, as my eyes trailed over the gathered group and I quickly counted them up - eighty three people had chosen to join the defense in total - I couldn’t help but linger on familiar faces. There were people who’d visited my shop, people I’d nodded at or greeted in the Hall, and people I knew much, much better than that. The people I’d trained in the use of poison what felt like lifetimes ago stood out. Yors, Emma, a cat beastkin, and an elf from among the rank of hunters. Then there was Dreven Hoffmann himself, another elf, a human, and Martha. I’d almost forgotten that Dreven was part of the training group. Back then, I hadn’t even bothered to ask for people’s names, and with how little the group had been required to do in the end let me put the entire thing behind me. It was actually Alys who introduced us in the end, and even then, when he approached me later inside my store it took me time to dredge up his name. Case in point, I still didn’t know the names of most of the others. I was going to fix that, my much improved attitude and lack of desire to continue separating myself from the town demanded at least that much, but I had a bigger problem at the moment. Literally. Martha was glaring at me like I’d personally offended her, and as she started to stomp her way over to me, I realized that was exactly what I’d done somehow. I had just opened my mouth to apologize for the threat Kiri and I had dragged right up to the town’s doorstep when the minotaur’s rumbling voice drowned out my own. “You didn’t tell me. First, you didn’t tell me who and what you are. Then you didn’t bother to tell me that you are in danger. I thought I was your friend, but apparently I’m the only one who felt that way,” the minotaur crossed her arms under her chest aggressively, still glaring. Everything I was about to say died a quick, quiet and undignified death. Yes, she was angry with me. Considerably so, from what I could tell. However, I’d completely misjudged the source of that anger. “I’m sorry. You are not the only one who felt that way. I… it is not a good excuse, but Kiri and I didn’t want anyone else to get sucked into the mire of our problems.” I winced at the dismissive snort that left her. “Obviously, that didn’t work out, but we tried.” She was still glaring. She was still angry. Thankfully, her stance softened ever so slightly as she leaned closer to me to mutter angrily. “Hiding shit from me stops here. I can’t help you or keep the town safe if you are holding things back. I’m not forgiving either of you yet. Not by a long shot. But I’m going to help protect my friends, and then you can work on earning my forgiveness.” With that, the minotaur turned around and stomped her way back to the group she’d been standing with, leaving me to suck in a deep, slightly tremulous breath. I hadn’t expected everyone to just forgive and forget immediately. That would have been ridiculously hopeful and naive. Still, to know that one of the people I genuinely considered a friend was that upset with me left me feeling off balance. Anyway, I forced myself to focus on the moment and swept my eyes over the group again. Most of the people gathered in front of me were on the older side of the mortal lifespans. A very large chunk of them were surprisingly well equipped, however. Their weapons and armor plainly bore age and use, but they were still kept in excellent condition and I could tell they felt supremely comfortable in their gear. Likewise, I noticed that more than a few had matching sets of armor, if not weapons. They all bore the symbol of the Snowdrop Kingdom too, so it wasn’t exactly hard to figure out where they got them. Now, I wasn’t particularly familiar with standing militaries of smaller kingdoms, or how they organized their ranks, but I was taken aback by how many of the uniformly armored individuals also showed trimming and other signs of high standing on their armor. Not noble standing, mind, but the kind of rank that was acknowledged through blood and suffering on the battlefield. That was a very pleasant surprise for me, and hopefully a much worse surprise for the approaching Wild Hunt. You might be reading a stolen copy. Visit Royal Road for the authentic version. Still, I wasn’t there to admire the hidden depths of my small frontier town. I was there to give the people in front of me an actual fighting chance. “I trust that the elders have explained to you what is happening? Good. I cannot thank you all enough for choosing to stand with Kiri, me, and our family. What I can do, however, is hand out these.” I pulled a box out of my storage bag, then passed it off to Nasha who bounced up to me excitedly and shot me a grin before moving to distribute the potions while I handed off three more boxes to Pen, Kiri, and Vren. “These potions are why I asked for all volunteers to gather today. They will provide you with a significant boost to your physical abilities, and while I can guarantee that they are safe to use, I do not yet know how effective they are. It is also risky to use a potion for the first time in life and death combat. That is why we are here to test things out, as well as do some training on how to handle poison safely afterwards.” The gathered volunteers seemed rather receptive to the idea if the way they eyed the potions greedily and with glee was any indication, and I couldn’t blame them. I believed, and continued to do so, that the potions were highly wasteful. They were still extremely valuable and not something people could typically get their hands on, doubly so when it came to the level of quality I’d insisted on while brewing them. This was also why the idea of testing the potions first pained me. I could produce four to five potions from a single brew, yes, but covering the needs of the entire group and then repeating the feat so everyone had a potion on hand for the ultimate clash between us and the Wild Hunt was a resource and time consumption I loathed. Unfortunately, that was a lesser evil compared to throwing away the lives of people willing to fight by our side, so work I did. I watched, amused, as people threw back the potions and then staggered when the bottled power swept through their bodies. There were no dramatic physical changes. No growing taller, or sprouting claws and scales. However, when they started testing their physical abilities, the grins on people’s faces were unmistakable. Weapons tore through the air with enough force to make it whine. People lifted logs, thoughtfully prepared by Alys ahead of time, that they would never be able to move on their own, with ease. I also had to groan and let my head drop into my hands when a dwarf enthusiastically taunted a wolfkin into punting him with enough strength to make him vanish into the treeline before the loud crack of dwarf on wood announced the collapse of a tree. The reckless idiot staggered back to us, laughing and no worse for wear. The idiot who’d kicked him whooped in celebration, then cringed when Martha brought a large fist down on his head and started verbally tearing into him. For a moment, I wondered if this was the group I wanted to bring to bear against a Wild Hunt, especially one led by my own mother, Kiri’s siblings, and a Summer Court unknown who hadn’t left their carriage yet. As I watched them devolve into various friendly competitions and increasingly reckless behavior, I felt an unexpectedly powerful fondness settle within my chest. They were certainly a colorful crowd, yes, but they were also the people who’d willingly decided to put themselves in danger to help protect my family. I wasn’t going to forget that in a hurry, and from a fond, satisfied grin Alys wore when she popped over to check on us, she shared my sentiment. _ We all had some way to contribute to averting the disaster headed our way. I had my alchemy and skill with poison. The latter was a potential threat to my own allies as well, but antidotes and training could mitigate that well enough. I didn’t have time to dole out said training myself, but the group I’d put through the wringer in preparation for facing the draconic eel were passing down everything they’d learned from me to this larger defense force, and I trusted them to do a good job. The kobolds had loudly protested my attempt to get them to sit out the combat, and had forced their way into joining the training our troops had organized. It wasn’t just poison handling they were drilling, since plenty of the townsfolk were trying to get back to full combat readiness after living regular, safe lives for a while, according to Martha. The minotaur was still frosty towards Kiri and me, but she didn’t extend that to our family, which I was thankful for, and she was also leading the training efforts, which I appreciated just as much. Soren had thrown himself into training as well, both with and apart from our volunteer army, and had even extracted four more potion vials from me to practice with the enhancements active a little more. He was another person I’d tried to convince into skipping out on direct combat, along with Amara, but both had chosen to ignore me. Alys looked at me like I was an idiot for even suggesting such things to her mother and father, and had looked like she was waiting for me to try and press her on leaving ahead of the Wild Hunt’s arrival again, but I wisely chose not to. I knew how stubborn my dragoness could be, and I didn’t want to get into a pointless argument she would win anyway. When she eventually realized as much, she looked so intensely proud of me that I felt embarrassed. She was also very cuddly that evening, which was always a plus! Something that amused me was that Amara was putting as much effort into preparing for the Wild Hunt as I was… and I had absolutely no idea what exactly she was doing. All I knew was that she’d commandeered my dragoness’ attention and that they spent most of their time in the torture juice fruit cavern. Every time I asked, Amara just looked smug and told me I was going to enjoy the surprise they were working on. It was Kiri that was suffering the most, however. The Winter fae had taken on the task of preparing her familiars for combat and, far more importantly, keeping an eye on the approaching Wild Hunt. She looked ever more stressed the more time she spent just watching them march on our home, and the fact that she lost whatever familiar she sent after them if they got too close to the marching fae was not helping. Thirteen birds had lost their lives before she resigned herself to only spying on them from afar, and each death had rocked the Winter Princess like a physical blow. I knew she would be fine, if only because Ritsu was constantly there and taking care of her at that point, but the sheer misery radiating off of her because of the deaths and the Wild Hunt in general made me desperately want to help her somehow. Unfortunately, there was simply nothing I could do but wait and take care of the threat when they were finally upon us. That day snuck up on us entirely too quickly, even if we’d been tracking their progress every step of the way. The Wild Hunt was finally within reach… And all any of us could hope was that we were genuinely ready.

  Chapter 175: Crushing Waves
  https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/135311/alchemist-of-the-wilds-an-ex-assassins-guide-to/chapter/3203951/chapter-175-crushing-waves

The Wild Hunt approached the same way they’d travelled for the past eight days it had taken them to crawl their way to our home: slowly, meticulously, and inexorably. Unlike the first time we spotted them it was the Summer cohort leading the way, with the carriage right up front this time, too. That still didn’t let us catch a glimpse of who was inside the stupid thing, but it did provide for an impressive show of power considering the fact that the carriage was clearing the way for the rest of the Wild Hunt. Before their visit, there was no easy path that would allow someone to reach Swiftband. Now, one was burned across the landscape. According to Kiri, the horse shaped fire elementals’ forms had flared up the moment they’d reached the forested portion of the path to our town, and their flames had gone from normal shades of red, yellow and orange to a blinding, brilliant gold. They’d then proceeded to clop ever onwards, incinerating every piece of greenery they came in contact with to ash instantaneously, to the point where a forest fire didn’t even have a chance to erupt. It was as much a show of might as it was of opulence, since the people travelling inside the carriage had yet to show themselves even now. We also noticed, because we’d spent the last day or so just relaxing and spying on the Hunt, that the Autumn cohort really didn’t like their Summer counterparts, starting with my mother. According to our Winter spymaster my mother had been glaring at the carriage every chance she got, but the rest of the fae under her command had chosen to follow her lead when Summer’s plan to burn a new path to Swiftband had been unveiled. The Winter cohort didn’t seem to care either way, but they’d retreated to the tail end of the procession and the two Royals had elected to trail behind their troops for good measure. The way they were eying the golden flames suggested they weren’t as indifferent as they tried to act too, at least to me. That’s around when our surveillance situation got even worse than it was before. Like they’d suddenly taken offense to being observed even from afar, whoever was killing Kiri’s familiars managed to take another three down in quick succession before she managed to pull them back. I was more annoyed about the pain that caused Kiri than the loss of visibility we suffered, since we could still track them based on the Summer carriage’s glow as they progressed through the forest. Still, this did mean that, when the furthest mutated manchineel grove from us suddenly had its wards shattered, we didn’t have eyes on what was happening there. We did see a brief flare of golden flames, but whether that meant that the grove had been reduced to cinders or not wasn’t something I could guess. Two more implosions of suddenly scattering concentrations of mana followed, letting us know that the other groves had been visited too, but then we were stuck waiting for the moment when we could finally stroll outside and get our own eyes on the Wild Hunt. It was not something I was looking forward to. Nor was I actually going to let any of them lay their eyes on me in turn until I absolutely had to. Until that happened we still had plausible deniability on our side and certain cards we could play if the Courts fell to temporary insanity and decided to go for diplomacy instead of their typical hamfisted approach to mortal settlement. Granted, that deniability was paper thin when we ran a little… experiment, before we lost sight of the Wild Hunt. Alys had indulged in her normal morning snack meant to help her grow and improve her bloodline, but we’d delayed her dose of my refined blood for a little bit, letting the sensation of our daughter drawing on my mana clutch me fully. It was subtle, and we only spotted it because we were looking for it, but my mother had stiffened and turned to look directly in our direction. This, at least, meant that the chances were good that we could get the Hunt to focus their assault on our home rather than on Swiftband. I didn’t have a single bad thing to say about Grafton’s work once he was forced to actually do something, but his wards still had nothing on the ones laid by The Molten Expanse herself, and that’s discounting the power source grandmother had gifted to us. Therefore, we wanted the Hunt’s attention. If the town itself got drawn into the conflict, then either something had gone very wrong or we’d gotten desperate enough that risking the lives of all the townsfolk was a reasonable decision to make. I really, really hoped things wouldn’t devolve to that point. Regardless, this was why, when Kiri’s ice mirrors offered us the perfect view of the Hunt emerging from the forest on the other side of the town from us, Alys immediately had some of the refined draconic materials, leaving the draw on my mana and essence to get powerful enough to catch my mother’s attention. We watched with bated breath as the procession left the forest completely, led by the Summer carriage still, before my mother trotted up to the fiery vehicle and thumped angrily on its side. This made sense to me, especially from how the plant matter still sizzled and let out puffs of smoke when the carriage pulled by fire elementals finally started its crossing, never mind that the elementals were now looking almost fully solid from how much they were trying to quiet and suppress their flames. My mother had stopped on the opposite bank of the river, now standing on a plot of ground that made it so there was nothing more than a stroll separating us, and continued to glare at the carriage until it had made the crossing as well. She motioned at a few of her Autumn troops to come forward and inspect the bridge, which they did, healing it from the damage the Summer cohort had inflicted on it, before all three Courts began to reorganize and mesh. At the very front stood a line of Winter fae, all of them looking feral and eager for combat. Animals had streamed out of the forest when it became impossible for them to conceal themselves, and so the fae were now surrounded by up to three familiars each. Some were relatively plain animals, some were exotic and clearly magical in nature, and some were outright monstrous in a way that told me someone had had far too much fun sculpting little nightmares for personal use. Or, not so little nightmares, actually. Two of the Winter soldiers smugly stood next to miniature behemoths of physical might and violence. One still bore lingering signs of having been a bear at some point, but so much of it was replaced by sickly looking scales and a myriad of mouths that were all slavering and gnashing at nothing that I couldn’t think of it as such. The other was surprisingly sleek looking and might have passed for a natural-born creature if the pangolin look-alike didn’t continuously spawn spikes that stabbed out of its skin in a way that made me flinch, leaving behind holes that slowly closed while giving us a glimpse of something writhing and squirming beneath the surface. I wanted absolutely nothing to do with Winter Court’s creations, and Kiri looked vaguely ill when she looked over the assembled animals with pity. Behind the Winter frontline was a row of Summer troops, followed by a layer of Autumn soldiers, before the same patterns repeated - Winter, Summer, Autumn at the tail end. What confused me a little was the proportions of the layers. The first three were by far more populous than the latter ones, particularly in the case of Winter. They had practically all of their soldiers out front, with barely enough to form a proper line in their repeated layer. Summer was front heavy, too, while Autumn was split about fifty-fifty between the two lines. Interestingly enough, the Winter siblings, after a brief and spirited chat with my mother, smugly made their way to the front too. She watched them with an inscrutable expression on her face before shaking her head and briefly addressing a fae woman who seemed to be in charge of leading the secondary Winter layer, before leisurely strolling over to the first Autumn line. And that was that! There had been no attempts to reach out, discuss things, or even demand our surrender. Their final preparations came in the form of the Winter cohort pulling on their helmets (and a whole lot of them chose to eschew that entirely, leaving them on their hips or attached to their saddles), and the Autumn fae’s armor growing up to conceal their heads. I was mildly interested to note that the grown helmets were not uniform, taking on the vague resemblance of various animals, presumably according to the wearer’s wishes, before Kiri’s brother raised a horn up to his lips. The deep, resonant wail of a Wild Hunt’s call to slaughter washed over everything, vibrating the very earth under our feet and forcing air out of people’s lungs. Fear attempted to grip me, surging into me not from deep within my chest but from the particles of mana that had been forced to flee before the Wild Hunt, and while I crushed it easily enough I saw the kobolds and Soren shuffle uncomfortably. Lilly’s hand briefly fell to a long, wicked-looking dagger she currently bore on her hip, fingers wrapping around its hilt until her scales went pale, but she managed to gather herself and release the weapon. My dragoness and her mother, on the other hand, just looked pissed off. In fact, Amara started giggling to herself maliciously while looking like she couldn’t wait to hurt each and every fae that her eyes swept across. Alys just looked like she could use a snack as she ran her tongue across her teeth in a way that normally told me I was going to have to get out of bed and fetch her some food if I didn’t want to have a pouty dragoness in my bed. And then the Wild Hunt charged. The Winter abominations were at the front. The familiars, goaded by their masters’ bloodlust, howled, yipped and made much more disturbing sounds as they charged straight for our home. I could only assume that the fae could sense the wall of mana that were our wards, but I was willing to bet that cracking the defenses of the groves had emboldened more than a few of them. Even through our defenses, I could feel the spells they were using at the edge of my awareness, so potent were they. I saw their effects easily enough too, as even the smallest of the familiars swelled in size and power. Maybe they were expecting them to be enough to crash straight through our wards. Maybe the tide of mana and violence directed our way would have been enough to bring low the defences of most mortal capital cities. There was also the fact that the groves were protected by gentle wards. Wards meant to do little more than bar passage and turn away curious or hungry animals. The wards protecting our home were definitely not gentle. The familiars slammed into our first line of defense, and instead of getting straight through it, bones snapped and lives were extinguished from the sheer force of their charge meeting an immovable surface. That’s when a wave of mana streamed up our defenses, briefly making them turn visible to the naked mortal eye, before it snapped outwards under my dragoness’ direct control. The Wild Hunt’s charge faltered, but they really didn’t have enough time to do more than stare as our retaliation slammed into them.

'I've never seen him like this…' Nicolo thought. "Hang on, Akyo," he whispered. "for us." Tachi stood by the door outside the room. "Tachi!" a voice cried. Ana arrived running. "What are you doing here? What's in that room?!" she demanded. He didn't answer. "I'll look for myself!" she said, but he stopped her before she could open the door. "You can't," he said. "Tachi… you're scaring me… who is it?" He still didn't answer, and she understood. "No… no, that's impossible." Her face turned pale. "It's not possible!" She grew angry. "Stop messing around, I need to see him!" She started crying, hitting her brother's chest. "I'm begging you… let me in…" she sobbed. "If I can't see him… it means there's no hope… and… I can't believe that!!" 'She's right…' Tachi thought. "Go…" he whispered. "What?" She hadn't heard. She looked up, and saw him. He was crying too. "Go in," he said. She did. Ana opened the door and entered the room. Nicolo, seated beside Akyo, saw her coming. 'Even he couldn't stop her,' he thought. "No…" she whispered when she saw Akyo. She approached the bed. "This is my fault," she murmured. She collapsed, tears pouring down her cheeks. "I'm the one who sent you there… I'm so sorry, Akyo…"

  10. The High Priestess Game
  Tác giả: Rahel Vega
  Tổng chương: 7
  Ngày cập nhật: N/A
  URL: https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/158804/the-high-priestess-game
▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓▓

  Mô tả: Rahel Vega has always known what comes next. Her tarot readings are never wrong. Her spirit guides never stay silent. Her clients leave with answers (even when they don’t like them). Until the cards turn on her. For weeks, one message keeps repeating: The Tower. No matter how often she asks, the answer doesn’t change. Something in her life is about to collapse. Tomorrow. And this time, the cards refuse to explain why.

───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  [Part 6] - Vol. 1 Ch. 6: Bad Hand
  https://www.royalroad.com/fiction/158804/the-high-priestess-game/chapter/3200012/part-6-vol-1-ch-6-bad-hand
